[30;1m127 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m128 | [0m[35mIn some specific cases, you might only want to catch the cancellation exception. This is[0m
[30;1m129 | [0m[35mtricky because each async framework has its own exception class for that and AnyIO[0m
[30;1m130 | [0m[35mcannot control which exception is raised in the task when it's cancelled. To work around[0m
[30;1m131 | [0m[35mthat, AnyIO provides a way to retrieve the exception class specific to the currently[0m
[30;1m132 | [0m[35mrunning async framework, using :func:`~get_cancelled_exc_class`::[0m
[30;1m133 | [0m[35m[0m

[30;1m153 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m154 | [0m[35mCapacity limiters are like semaphores except that a single borrower (the current task by[0m
[30;1m155 | [0m[35mdefault) can only hold a single token at a time. It is also possible to borrow a token[0m
[30;1m156 | [0m[35mon behalf of any arbitrary object, so long as that object is hashable.[0m

[30;1m112 | [0m[35mA condition is basically a combination of an event and a lock. It first acquires a lock[0m
[30;1m113 | [0m[35mand then waits for a notification from the event. Once the condition receives a[0m
[30;1m114 | [0m[35mnotification, it releases the lock. The notifying task can also choose to wake up more[0m
[30;1m115 | [0m[35mthan one listener at once, or even all of them.[0m
[30;1m116 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m117 | [0m[35mLike :class:`Lock`, :class:`Condition` also requires that the task which locked it also[0m
[30;1m118 | [0m[35mthe one to release it.[0m

[30;1m77 | [0m[35m-----[0m
[30;1m78 | [0m[35m[0m
[30;1m79 | [0m[35mLocks are used to guard shared resources to ensure sole access to a single task at once.[0m

[30;1m45 | [0m[35mSemaphores are used for limiting access to a shared resource. A semaphore starts with a[0m
[30;1m46 | [0m[35mmaximum value, which is decremented each time the semaphore is acquired by a task and[0m

[30;1m6 | [0m[35mA *task* is a unit of execution that lets you do many things concurrently that need[0m
[30;1m7 | [0m[35mwaiting on. This works so that while you can have any number of tasks, the asynchronous[0m
[30;1m8 | [0m[35mevent loop can only run one of them at a time. When the task encounters an ``await``[0m
[30;1m9 | [0m[35mstatement that requires the task to sleep until something happens, the event loop is[0m
[30;1m10 | [0m[35mthen free to work on another task. When the thing the first task was waiting is[0m
[30;1m11 | [0m[35mcomplete, the event loop will resume the execution of that task on the first opportunity[0m

[30;1m47 | [0m[35mSometimes it is very useful to be able to wait until a task has successfully initialized[0m

[30;1m49 | [0m[35mlistener and then signal the caller that initialization is done. That way, the caller[0m
[30;1m50 | [0m[35mcan now start another task that depends on that service being up and running. Also, if[0m
